<div id="review_2056266777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2056266777" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64860542-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488107392p2/64860542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2056266777?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/64860542-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64860542-emma?shelf=unfinished-series">unfinished-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2056266777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10274559839336000167">Edited to add -- at the time of this edit only 3 books in the series are out with the third one being significantly frustrating. Even more annoying is the fact the author plans a total of 6-9 books total but is not even working on book 4. This is according to her own website. So it looks like it could be more than 6 years before this is completed. By then I won't remember or care much. <br/>---------------------------<br/>4.5* - I simply could not put it down.<br/><br/>This book was suggested to me by amazon becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText10274559839336000167" style="display:none">Edited to add -- at the time of this edit only 3 books in the series are out with the third one being significantly frustrating. Even more annoying is the fact the author plans a total of 6-9 books total but is not even working on book 4. This is according to her own website. So it looks like it could be more than 6 years before this is completed. By then I won't remember or care much. <br />---------------------------<br />4.5* - I simply could not put it down.<br /><br />This book was suggested to me by amazon because of some M/M fantasy I had read. I read the blurb and declined to read it as I have never really been into vampires and BDSM generally turns me off. The blurb for this book does not lie. But it in no way prepared me for how rivetted I would be. After I got to the end I tried to figure out what the hell I had just read and why I liked it. I'm not really able to answer that but here goes nothing.<br /><br /><b>What it was: </b>The story of Matthew, a young vampire who knows little of his kind, getting trapped by Tarrick a very old incubus. Told entirely from Matthews point of view we learn about the paranormal world as he does, bit by teeny bit. We get a lot of violence and a lot of sex. <br /><br /><b>What it was not: </b><br /><br />BDSM. While there is a sexual relationship with a slave and master that role is not for sexual gratification alone. There are damn good reasons why Matthew is held prisoner and why Tarrick is trying to break his will that have zero to do with sex or personal kinks.<br /><br />M/M romance. First off there is no romance. There is M/M sex but the incubi will have sex with anything for any reason, wherever and whenever they want. And that is the biggest mind fuck of the book in that we can not figure out what Tarrick is thinking or feeling. Ascribing human motives or feelings to him is pointless because he does not work like we do. Also the most caring sex in the book is arguably M/F. Granted most of it is not described but its role is quite important to the story so it can't be glossed over. (For many M/M readers that will push this into the no-go zone.)<br /><br />erotica - well okay it probably is erotica to some but that sure is not me. I read a few reviews that complain about the M/M scenes being less steamy than the M/F ones but I suspect that is because they are not meant to be steamy. They are graphic and often twisted. But this is not a love affair and there is dubious consent at best.<br /><br />gay/bisexual/lgbtq* - These are not humans so the terms just don't make much sense. If anything the Incubi are bisexual but that implies they are limited by something. They aren't. In the third book we find out that one particular incubus has had sex with all manner of beings including but certainly not limited to humans, vampires, mermaids, trolls, demons, demigods, and centaurs. They are way past worrying about labels.<br /><br /><b>Why I liked it: </b> A lot of the time I felt like I was in a Greek myth. The actions were just that fucked up and insane. However the internal logic worked. I liked that it was built up slowly but never felt like a character had certain powers just to make things easier on the author. What I call "going through the transporter backwards syndrome". (I really hate GTTBS). Even though Tarrick's full motives and feelings are not revealed I always felt the author knew what they were and kept him consistent. I think that is important with a character as inscrutable as he is. Matthew held onto a lot of his human nature while still having his paranormal nature too. There was enough human about him I felt I could relate to him and I felt so bad for him. I like a book that can keep me guessing right to the end. I figured Matthew would still be with us at the end but in what shape and under what conditions I still was not sure of even as the big battles were being waged. <br /><br />There were a few things I was less keen on but they were pretty minor. I'm not at all sure what the writer's obsession with clothing descriptions is. Seriously weird. And it only gets weirder by the third book. I think her day job might be for clothing retailer. <br /><br />This book is part of an incomplete series and as such the story is not over at the end of this book. Still it does end at a suitable place and if you didn't love it enough to read book 2 I don't think you would be frustrated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10274559839336000167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3AKUK92JMwYOSe9KGqhruc3QH8UNrKNN23Xfu29xEz5t8A+wxGli42isHzteu+bmrJ09wIFJReOYgZZLTE0W/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('a3lA72EFneWytEqzDtQHUvEy6jWfDV5DPr577vNGYQjai9t0eOXMANRRusJKx4oNkH/IMBPouO19SjIe0Hpkyg==')})
  }

Restless and heartsick, he returns to wandering, traveling from settlement to settlement, delivering tokens of love, not death.  Among his Order brethren at Ashford, he rediscovers the joy of careless pleasures and the thrill of knowing he\'ll be gone in the morning. But one assassin isn\'t so easily dismissed. Proud, powerful, and a self-centered prick, Sentinel Venali is everything Trey despises. But he fucks like there\'s no tomorrow, and right now, sex with no strings attached is exactly what Trey needs.  When fellow Order elves begin to take their own lives, the depth of the damage done by the war becomes apparent.  Trey has watched those around him buckle beneath their fears, powerless to stop their self-destructive path. He knows some cries for help are silent. And few need help more than the damaged Venali.  Tomorrow, Trey will be gone. Because staying means loving, and his cracked heart cannot withstand another break.  If only it were that simple to say goodbye.  ***  Trey\'s novella takes place after events in the Silk &amp; Steel trilogy. For the best experience, please read the Silk &amp; Steel trilogy first. This novella does contain spoilers for the Silk &amp; Steel series of novels.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17095187261781391530\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
